window['backfillParam']['pl_tmodn']
=
3;








}






function
google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Nirvana_(band)';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"band,nirvana,(,_,),";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Nirvana</b>
was
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
formed
by
singer/guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Kurt
Cobain</a>
and
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Krist_Novoselic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Krist
Novoselic">Krist
Novoselic</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Aberdeen,_Washington?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aberdeen,
Washington">Aberdeen,
Washington</a>
in
1987.
Nirvana
went
through
a
succession
of
drummers,
the
longest-lasting
being
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Grohl">Dave
Grohl</a>,
who
joined
the
band
in
1990.
Despite
releasing
only
three
full-length
studio
albums
in
their
seven-year
career,
Nirvana
has
come
to
be
regarded
as
one
of
the
most
influential
and
important
rock
bands
of
the
modern
era.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nirvana_bio_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nirvana_bio-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
late
1980s
Nirvana
established
itself
as
part
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Seattle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seattle">Seattle</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Grunge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grunge">grunge</a>
scene,
releasing
its
first
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bleach_(Nirvana_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bleach
(Nirvana
album)">Bleach</a></i>
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Independent_record_label?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Independent
record
label">independent
record
label</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Sub_Pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sub
Pop">Sub
Pop</a>
in
1989.
The
band
eventually
came
to
develop
a
sound
that
relied
on
dynamic
contrasts,
often
between
quiet
verses
and
loud,
heavy
choruses.
After
signing
to
major
label
<a
href="/wiki/DGC_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DGC
Records">DGC
Records</a>,
Nirvana
found
unexpected
success
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Smells_Like_Teen_Spirit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit">Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit</a>&quot;,
the
first
single
from
the
band's
second
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nevermind?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nevermind">Nevermind</a></i>
(1991).
Nirvana's
sudden
success
widely
popularized
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>
as
a
whole,
and
the
band's
frontman
Cobain
found
himself
referred
to
in
the
media
as
the
&quot;spokesman
of
a
generation&quot;,
with
Nirvana
being
considered
the
&quot;flagship
band&quot;
of
<a
href="/wiki/Generation_X?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Generation
X">Generation
X</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nirvana's
third
and
final
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Utero_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Utero
(album)">In
Utero</a></i>
(1993),
featured
an
abrasive,
less-mainstream
sound
and
challenged
the
group's
audience.
The
album
did
not
match
the
sales
figures
of
<i>Nevermind</i>
but
was
still
a
critical
and
commercial
success.
Nirvana's
brief
run
ended
following
the
<a
href="/wiki/Death_of_Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Death
of
Kurt
Cobain">death
of
Kurt
Cobain</a>
in
1994,
but
various
posthumous
releases
have
been
issued
since,
overseen
by
Novoselic,
Grohl,
and
Cobain's
widow
<a
href="/wiki/Courtney_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Courtney
Love">Courtney
Love</a>.</p>








<p>Since
its
debut,
the
band
has
sold
over
25
million
records
in
the
United
States
alone,
and
over
75
million
records
worldwide,
making
them
one
of
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">the
best-selling
music
artists</a>
in
history.
Four
of
their
albums,
two
studio
and
two
live,
have
reached
the
number
one
spot
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
chart.
In
the
years
since
the
band's
breakup,
Nirvana
has
been
ranked
highly
on
several
lists
by
various
publications
as
one
of
the
greatest
artists
of
all
time.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
described
Nirvana's
influence
as
having
&quot;kicked
in&quot;
the
1990s
as
a
musical
era,<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
adding
that
their
music
&quot;guaranteed
the
nineties
would
not
suck,&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
claimed
that
the
band
&quot;transformed
rock
for
a
generation.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
the
magazine,
&quot;few
bands
in
rock
history
have
had
a
more
immediate
and
tangible
impact
on
their
contemporary
pop
musical
landscape
than
Nirvana
did
in
the
early
Nineties.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Nirvana
is
set
to
be
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2014,
the
band's
first
year
of
eligibility;
the
museum's
biography
of
the
band
states
that
Nirvana
&quot;start[ed]
a
rock
revolution&quot;
and
&quot;remain
an
enduring
influence
and
challenge&quot;,
before
declaring
them
&quot;proof
that
the
right
band
with
the
right
noise
can
change
the
world.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
style="overflow:hidden;height:;">








&nbsp;







</div>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_early_years">Formation
and
early
years</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
early
years">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Cobain
and
Novoselic
met
while
attending
Aberdeen
High,
although
they
never
connected,
according
to
Cobain.<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
pair
eventually
became
friends
while
frequenting
the
practice
space
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Melvins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Melvins">Melvins</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
wanted
to
form
a
band
with
Novoselic,
but
Novoselic
did
not
respond
to
his
requests,
which
included
giving
him
a
demo
tape
of
his
project
<a
href="/wiki/Fecal_Matter_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fecal
Matter
(band)">Fecal
Matter</a>.
Three
years
after
the
two
first
met,
Novoselic
notified
Cobain
that
he
had
finally
listened
to
the
Fecal
Matter
demo
Cobain
had
given
him,
and
suggested
they
start
a
group.
The
pair
recruited
Bob
McFadden
on
drums,
but
after
a
month
the
project
fell
apart.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
late
1987,
Cobain
and
Novoselic
recruited
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Aaron_Burckhard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aaron
Burckhard">Aaron
Burckhard</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
three
practiced
material
from
Cobain's
Fecal
Matter
tape,
but
started
writing
new
material
soon
after
forming.<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
its
initial
months,
the
band
went
through
a
series
of
names,
starting
with
Skid
Row
and
including
Pen
Cap
Chew,
Bliss,
and
Ted
Ed
Fred.
The
group
finally
settled
on
Nirvana,
which
Cobain
said
was
chosen
because
&quot;I
wanted
a
name
that
was
kind
of
beautiful
or
nice
and
pretty
instead
of
a
mean,
raunchy
punk
name
like
the
<a
href="/wiki/Angry_Samoans?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angry
Samoans">Angry
Samoans</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
Novoselic
and
Cobain
having
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/Tacoma,_Washington?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tacoma,
Washington">Tacoma</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Olympia,_Washington?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Olympia,
Washington">Olympia,
Washington</a>,
respectively,
the
two
temporarily
lost
contact
with
Burckhard.
The
pair
instead
practiced
with
<a
href="/wiki/Dale_Crover?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dale
Crover">Dale
Crover</a>
of
the
Melvins,
and
Nirvana
recorded
its
first
demos
in
January
1988.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
early
1988,
Crover
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/San_Francisco?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Francisco">San
Francisco</a>
but
recommended
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Foster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Foster">Dave
Foster</a>
to
the
band
as
his
replacement
on
drums.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Foster's
tenure
with
Nirvana
lasted
only
a
few
months;
during
a
stint
in
jail,
he
was
replaced
by
a
returning
Burckhard,
who
himself
didn't
stay
with
the
band
after
telling
Cobain
he
was
too
hung
over
to
practice
one
day.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
and
Novoselic
put
an
ad
in
Seattle
music
publication
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Rocket_(newspaper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Rocket
(newspaper)">The
Rocket</a></i>
seeking
a
replacement
drummer
which
only
yielded
unsatisfactory
responses.
Meanwhile,
a
mutual
friend
introduced
them
to
<a
href="/wiki/Chad_Channing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chad
Channing">Chad
Channing</a>,
and
the
three
musicians
agreed
to
jam
together.
Channing
continued
to
jam
with
Cobain
and
Novoselic,
although
the
drummer
noted,
&quot;They
never
actually
said
'Ok,
you're
in.'&quot;,
and
Channing
played
his
first
show
with
the
group
that
May.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_releases">Early
releases</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Early
releases">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Nirvana
released
its
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Love_Buzz?qsrc=3044#Nirvana"
title="Love
Buzz">Love
Buzz</a>&quot;,
in
November
1988
on
the
Seattle
<a
href="/wiki/Independent_record_label?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Independent
record
label">independent
record
label</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Sub_Pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sub
Pop">Sub
Pop</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
following
month,
the
band
began
recording
its
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bleach_(Nirvana_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bleach
(Nirvana
album)">Bleach</a></i>,
with
local
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Endino?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Endino">Jack
Endino</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Bleach</i>
was
highly
influenced
by
the
heavy
dirge-rock
of
the
Melvins
and
<a
href="/wiki/Mudhoney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mudhoney">Mudhoney</a>,
1980s
punk
rock,
and
the
1970s
<a
href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heavy
metal
music">heavy
metal</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Sabbath">Black
Sabbath</a>.
Novoselic
said
in
a
2001
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
that
the
band
had
played
a
tape
in
their
van
while
on
tour
that
had
an
album
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Smithereens?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Smithereens">The
Smithereens</a>
on
one
side
and
an
album
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Black_metal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
metal">black
metal</a>
band
<a
href="/wiki/Celtic_Frost?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Celtic
Frost">Celtic
Frost</a>
on
the
other,
and
noted
that
the
combination
probably
played
an
influence
as
well.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
money
for
the
recording
sessions
for
<i>Bleach</i>,
listed
as
$606.17
on
the
album
sleeve,
was
supplied
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jason_Everman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jason
Everman">Jason
Everman</a>,
who
was
subsequently
brought
into
the
band
as
the
second
guitarist.
Though
Everman
did
not
actually
play
on
the
album,
he
received
a
credit
on
<i>Bleach</i>
because,
according
to
Novoselic,
they
&quot;wanted
to
make
him
feel
more
at
home
in
the
band&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
Just
prior
to
the
album's
release,
Nirvana
insisted
on
signing
an
extended
contract
with
Sub
Pop,
making
the
band
the
first
to
do
so
with
the
label.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Following
the
release
of
<i>Bleach</i>
in
June
1989,
Nirvana
embarked
on
its
first
national
tour,<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
album
became
a
favorite
of
<a
href="/wiki/College_radio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="College
radio"
class="mw-redirect">college
radio</a>
stations.<sup
id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_review_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_review-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
Due
to
increasing
dissatisfaction
with
Everman
over
the
course
of
the
tour,
Nirvana
canceled
the
last
few
dates
and
drove
back
to
Washington.
No
one
told
Everman
he
was
fired
at
the
time,
while
Everman
later
claimed
that
he
actually
quit
the
group.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
Sub
Pop
did
not
promote
<i>Bleach</i>
as
much
as
other
releases,
it
was
a
steady
seller,<sup
id="cite_ref-Azerrad134_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Azerrad134-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
had
initial
sales
of
40,000
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
Cobain
was
upset
by
the
label's
lack
of
promotion
and
distribution
for
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-Azerrad134_27-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Azerrad134-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
late
1989,
the
band
recorded
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blew_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blew
(EP)">Blew</a></i>
EP
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Fisk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Fisk">Steve
Fisk</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
a
late
1989
interview,
Cobain
noted
that
the
band's
music
was
changing.
He
said,
&quot;The
early
songs
were
really
angry
...
But
as
time
goes
on
the
songs
are
getting
poppier
and
poppier
as
I
get
happier
and
happier.
The
songs
are
now
about
conflicts
in
relationships,
emotional
things
with
other
human
beings&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
April
1990,
the
band
began
working
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Vig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Vig">Butch
Vig</a>
at
Smart
Studios
in
<a
href="/wiki/Madison,_Wisconsin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison,
Wisconsin">Madison,
Wisconsin</a>
on
recordings
for
the
follow-up
to
<i>Bleach</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
sessions,
Cobain
and
Novoselic
became
disenchanted
with
Channing's
drumming,
and
Channing
expressed
frustration
at
not
being
actively
involved
in
songwriting.
As
bootlegs
of
Nirvana's
demos
with
Vig
began
to
circulate
in
the
music
industry
and
draw
attention
from
major
labels,
Channing
left
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
July,
the
band
recorded
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sliver_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sliver
(song)">Sliver</a>&quot;
with
Mudhoney
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Dan_Peters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dan
Peters">Dan
Peters</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nirvana
asked
Dale
Crover
to
fill
in
on
drums
for
a
seven-date
American
West
Coast
tour
with
<a
href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sonic
Youth">Sonic
Youth</a>
that
August.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
September
1990,
<a
href="/wiki/Buzz_Osborne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buzz
Osborne">Buzz
Osborne</a>
of
the
Melvins
introduced
the
band
to
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Grohl">Dave
Grohl</a>,
who
was
looking
for
a
new
band
following
the
sudden
break-up
of
Washington,
D.C.
<a
href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hardcore
punk">hardcore
punks</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Scream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scream
(band)">Scream</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
few
days
after
arriving
in
Seattle,
Novoselic
and
Cobain
auditioned
Grohl,
with
Novoselic
later
stating,
&quot;We
knew
in
two
minutes
that
he
was
the
right
drummer&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Mainstream_success">Mainstream
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Mainstream
success">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Disenchanted
with
Sub
Pop
and
with
the
Smart
Studios
sessions
generating
interest,
Nirvana
decided
to
look
for
a
deal
with
a
major
record
label
since
no
indie
label
could
buy
the
group
out
of
its
contract.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
Following
repeated
recommendations
by
Sonic
Youth's
<a
href="/wiki/Kim_Gordon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kim
Gordon">Kim
Gordon</a>,
Nirvana
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/DGC_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DGC
Records">DGC
Records</a>
in
1990.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
subsequently
began
recording
its
first
major
label
album,
<i>Nevermind</i>.
The
group
was
offered
a
number
of
producers
to
choose
from,
but
ultimately
held
out
for
Butch
Vig.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
Rather
than
recording
at
Vig's
Madison
studio
as
they
had
in
1990,
production
shifted
to
<a
href="/wiki/Sound_City_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
City
Studios">Sound
City
Studios</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Van_Nuys,_Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Van
Nuys,
Los
Angeles">Van
Nuys,
Los
Angeles</a>,
California.
For
two
months,
the
band
worked
through
a
variety
of
songs
in
its
catalog.
Some
of
the
songs,
such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_Bloom?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Bloom">In
Bloom</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Breed&quot;,
had
been
in
Nirvana's
repertoire
for
years,
while
others,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/On_a_Plain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="On
a
Plain">On
a
Plain</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Stay
Away,&quot;
lacked
finished
lyrics
until
mid-way
through
the
recording
process.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
recording
sessions
were
completed,
Vig
and
the
band
set
out
to
mix
the
album.
However,
the
recording
sessions
had
run
behind
schedule
and
the
resulting
mixes
were
deemed
unsatisfactory.
<a
href="/wiki/Slayer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slayer">Slayer</a>
mixer
<a
href="/wiki/Andy_Wallace_(producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Andy
Wallace
(producer)">Andy
Wallace</a>
was
brought
in
to
create
the
final
mix.
After
the
album's
release,
members
of
Nirvana
expressed
dissatisfaction
with
the
polished
sound
the
mixer
had
given
<i>Nevermind</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Initially,
DGC
Records
was
hoping
to
sell
250,000
copies
of
<i>Nevermind</i>,
which
was
the
same
level
they
had
achieved
with
Sonic
Youth's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Goo_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goo
(album)">Goo</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
the
album's
first
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Smells_Like_Teen_Spirit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit">Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit</a>&quot;
quickly
gained
momentum,
thanks
in
part
to
significant
airplay
of
the
song's
music
video
on
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>.
As
it
toured
Europe
during
late
1991,
the
band
found
that
its
shows
were
dangerously
oversold,
that
television
crews
were
becoming
a
constant
presence
onstage,
and
that
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;
was
almost
omnipresent
on
radio
and
music
television.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
Christmas
1991,
<i>Nevermind</i>
was
selling
400,000
copies
a
week
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
January
1992,
the
album
displaced
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Jackson">Michael
Jackson</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Michael_Jackson_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dangerous
(Michael
Jackson
album)">Dangerous</a></i>
at
number
one
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>
album
charts,
and
also
topped
the
charts
in
numerous
other
countries.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
month
<i>Nevermind</i>
reached
number
one,
<i>Billboard</i>
proclaimed,
&quot;Nirvana
is
that
rare
band
that
has
everything:
critical
acclaim,
industry
respect,
pop
radio
appeal,
and
a
rock-solid
college/alternative
base.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
would
eventually
sell
over
seven
million
copies
in
the
United
States,<sup
id="cite_ref-SoundScan_sales_47-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SoundScan_sales-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
over
30
million
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Citing
exhaustion,
Nirvana
decided
not
to
undertake
another
American
tour
in
support
of
<i>Nevermind</i>,
instead
opting
to
make
only
a
handful
of
performances
later
that
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March
1992,
Cobain
sought
to
reorganize
the
group's
songwriting
royalties
(which
to
this
point
had
been
split
equally)
so
that
they
were
more
representative
of
the
fact
that
he
wrote
the
majority
of
the
music.
Grohl
and
Novoselic
did
not
object
to
Cobain's
request,
but
when
the
frontman
asked
for
the
agreement
to
be
retroactive
to
the
release
of
<i>Nevermind</i>,
the
disagreements
between
the
two
sides
came
close
to
breaking
up
the
band.
After
a
week
of
tension,
Cobain
ended
up
receiving
a
retroactive
share
of
75
percent
of
the
royalties,
and
bad
feelings
about
the
situation
remained
within
the
group
afterward.<sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
Amid
rumors
that
the
band
was
disbanding
due
to
Cobain's
health,
Nirvana
headlined
the
closing
night
of
England's
1992
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Reading
Festival</a>,
where
Cobain
personally
programmed
the
performance
lineup.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nirvana's
performance
at
Reading
is
often
regarded
by
the
press
as
one
of
the
most
memorable
of
the
group's
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
few
days
later,
Nirvana
performed
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
where,
despite
the
network's
refusal
to
let
the
band
play
the
new
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rape_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rape
Me">Rape
Me</a>&quot;
during
the
broadcast,
Cobain
strummed
and
sang
the
first
few
bars
of
the
song
before
breaking
into
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lithium_(Nirvana_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lithium
(Nirvana
song)">Lithium</a>&quot;.
At
the
ceremony,
the
band
received
awards
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Video">Best
Alternative
Video</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_New_Artist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
for
Best
New
Artist">Best
New
Artist</a>
categories.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>DGC
had
hoped
to
have
a
new
Nirvana
album
by
the
band
ready
for
a
late
1992
holiday
season
release;
since
work
on
it
proceeded
slowly,
the
label
released
the
compilation
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Incesticide?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Incesticide">Incesticide</a></i>
in
December
1992.<sup
id="cite_ref-goldmine_55-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goldmine-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
joint
venture
between
DGC
and
Sub
Pop,
<i>Incesticide</i>
collected
various
rare
Nirvana
recordings
and
was
intended
to
provide
the
material
for
a
better
price
and
at
better
quality
than
was
available
via
bootleg
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-Azerrad.2C_1994._p._294_56-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Azerrad.2C_1994._p._294-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
<i>Nevermind</i>
had
been
out
for
15
months
and
had
yielded
a
fourth
single
in
&quot;In
Bloom&quot;
by
that
point,
Geffen/DGC
opted
not
to
heavily
promote
<i>Incesticide</i>,
which
was
certified
gold
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
Industry
Association
of
America">Recording
Industry
Association
of
America</a>
the
following
February.<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="In_Utero.2C_final_months.2C_and_Cobain.27s_death"><i>In
Utero</i>,
final
months,
and
Cobain's
death</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
In
Utero,
final
months,
and
Cobain's
death">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
boilerplate

also:

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

of
Kurt
Cobain">Death
of
Kurt
Cobain</a>







</div>

class="thumb
tright">

</div>
Cobain's
house
where
he
died.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
February
1993,
Nirvana
released
<a
href="/wiki/Puss/Oh,_the_Guilt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Puss/Oh,
the
Guilt">&quot;Puss&quot;/&quot;Oh,
the
Guilt&quot;</a>,
a
split
single
with
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jesus_Lizard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Jesus
Lizard">The
Jesus
Lizard</a>,
on
the
independent
label
<a
href="/wiki/Touch_and_Go_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touch
and
Go
Records">Touch
&amp;
Go</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-goldmine_55-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goldmine-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
Meanwhile,
the
group
chose
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Albini?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Albini">Steve
Albini</a>,
who
had
a
reputation
as
a
principled
and
opinionated
individual
in
the
American
<a
href="/wiki/Independent_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Independent
music">indie
music</a>
scene,
to
record
its
third
album.
While
there
was
speculation
that
the
band
chose
Albini
to
record
the
album
due
to
his
underground
credentials,<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
insisted
that
Albini's
sound
was
simply
the
one
he
had
always
wanted
Nirvana
to
have:
a
&quot;natural&quot;
recording
without
layers
of
studio
trickery.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nirvana
traveled
to
<a
href="/wiki/Pachyderm_Studio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pachyderm
Studio">Pachyderm
Studio</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Cannon_Falls,_Minnesota?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cannon
Falls,
Minnesota">Cannon
Falls,
Minnesota</a>
in
that
February
to
record
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-Gaar40_60-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Gaar40-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
sessions
with
Albini
were
productive
and
notably
quick,
and
the
album
was
recorded
and
mixed
in
two
weeks
for
a
cost
of
$25,000.<sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Several
weeks
after
the
completion
of
the
recording
sessions,
stories
ran
in
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chicago
Tribune">Chicago
Tribune</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Newsweek?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>
that
quoted
sources
claiming
DGC
considered
the
album
&quot;unreleasable&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
a
result,
fans
began
to
believe
that
the
band's
creative
vision
might
be
compromised
by
their
label.<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
the
stories
about
DGC
shelving
the
album
were
untrue,
the
band
actually
was
unhappy
with
certain
aspects
of
Albini's
mixes.
Specifically,
they
thought
the
bass
levels
were
too
low,<sup
id="cite_ref-FrickeRS1994_64-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FrickeRS1994-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Cobain
felt
that
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Heart-Shaped_Box?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heart-Shaped
Box">Heart-Shaped
Box</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_Apologies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Apologies">All
Apologies</a>&quot;
did
not
sound
&quot;perfect&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
Longtime
<a
href="/wiki/R.E.M.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a>
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Scott_Litt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Litt">Scott
Litt</a>
was
called
in
to
help
remix
those
two
songs,
with
Cobain
adding
additional
instrumentation
and
backing
vocals.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/In_Utero_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Utero
(album)">In
Utero</a></i>
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
album
chart
in
September
1993.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Time
(magazine)">Time</a></i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
<a
href="/wiki/Christopher_John_Farley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christopher
John
Farley">Christopher
John
Farley</a>
wrote
in
his
review
of
the
album,
&quot;Despite
the
fears
of
some
alternative-music
fans,
Nirvana
hasn't
gone
mainstream,
though
this
potent
new
album
may
once
again
force
the
mainstream
to
go
Nirvana.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>In
Utero</i>
went
on
to
sell
over
3.5
million
copies
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-SoundScan_sales_47-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SoundScan_sales-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Simultaneous
with
the
release
of
the
album,
Nirvana
was
recording
the
video
for
&quot;Heart-Shaped
Box&quot;
with
director
<a
href="/wiki/Anton_Corbijn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anton
Corbijn">Anton
Corbijn</a>,
based
on
a
detailed
treatment
prepared
by
Cobain.
The
video,
featuring
an
old
man
wearing
a
Santa-hat
who
ascends
a
ladder
and
affixes
himself
to
a
crucifix,
an
obese
angel
modeled
after
the
<a
href="/wiki/Visible_Human_Project?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Visible
Human
Project">Visible
Man</a>
angel
appearing
on
the
cover
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Utero_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Utero
(album)">In
Utero</a></i>,
and
a
tree
fruiting
fetuses,
has
been
interpreted
as
an
allegory
of
Heroin
addiction,
and
is
&quot;more
or
less
acknowledged
as
the
apical
manifestation
of
Kurt
Cobain's
highly
personal
alphabet
of
psychological
symbolism.&quot;
<sup
id="cite_ref-joyfulnoiserecordings.com_69-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-joyfulnoiserecordings.com-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
There
is
some
question
as
to
whether
or
not
the
old
man
appearing
in
the
video
is
actually
<a
href="/wiki/William_S._Burroughs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="William
S.
Burroughs">William
S.
Burroughs</a>.
<sup
id="cite_ref-joyfulnoiserecordings.com_69-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-joyfulnoiserecordings.com-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
video
won
multiple
awards
at
<a
href="/wiki/1994_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1994
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">1994's
MTV
Video
Awards</a>.</p>








<p>That
October,
Nirvana
embarked
on
its
first
tour
of
the
United
States
in
two
years.
For
the
tour,
the
band
added
<a
href="/wiki/Pat_Smear?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pat
Smear">Pat
Smear</a>
of
the
punk
rock
band
<a
href="/wiki/Germs_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Germs
(band)">Germs</a>
as
a
second
guitarist.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
November
1993,
Nirvana
recorded
a
performance
for
the
television
program
<i><a
href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Unplugged">MTV
Unplugged</a></i>.
Augmented
by
Smear
and
cellist
<a
href="/wiki/Lori_Goldston?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lori
Goldston">Lori
Goldston</a>,
the
band
sought
to
veer
from
the
typical
approach
to
the
show,
opting
to
stay
away
from
playing
its
most
recognizable
songs.
Instead,
Nirvana
performed
several
covers,
and
invited
<a
href="/wiki/Cris_Kirkwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cris
Kirkwood">Cris</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Curt_Kirkwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Curt
Kirkwood">Curt
Kirkwood</a>
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Meat_Puppets?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Meat
Puppets">Meat
Puppets</a>
to
join
the
group
for
renditions
of
three
of
their
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-diperna_unplugged_71-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-diperna_unplugged-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
early
1994,
the
band
embarked
on
a
European
tour.
Nirvana's
final
concert
took
place
in
Munich,
Germany,
on
March
1.
In
Rome,
on
the
morning
of
March
4,
Cobain's
wife,
<a
href="/wiki/Courtney_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Courtney
Love">Courtney
Love</a>,
found
Cobain
unconscious
in
their
hotel
room
and
he
was
rushed
to
the
hospital.
A
doctor
from
the
hospital
told
a
press
conference
that
Cobain
had
reacted
to
a
combination
of
prescription
<a
href="/wiki/Rohypnol?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rohypnol"
class="mw-redirect">Rohypnol</a>
and
alcohol.
The
rest
of
the
tour
was
canceled.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
ensuing
weeks,
Cobain's
<a
href="/wiki/Heroin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heroin">heroin</a>
addiction
resurfaced.
An
intervention
was
organized,
and
Cobain
was
convinced
to
admit
himself
into
drug
rehabilitation.
After
less
than
a
week
in
rehabilitation,
Cobain
climbed
over
the
wall
of
the
facility
and
took
a
plane
back
to
Seattle.
A
week
later,
on
Friday,
April
8,
1994,
Cobain
was
found
dead
of
a
possible
self-inflicted
shotgun
wound
to
the
head
at
his
Seattle
home.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Aftermath_and_posthumous_releases">Aftermath
and
posthumous
releases</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Aftermath
and
posthumous
releases">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
August
1994,
DGC
announced
that
a
double
album
titled
<i>Verse
Chorus
Verse</i>
featuring
live
material
from
throughout
the
group's
career
on
one
CD
and
its
<i>MTV
Unplugged</i>
performance
on
another
was
due
for
release
that
November.<sup
id="cite_ref-goldmine_55-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goldmine-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
Novoselic
and
Grohl
found
assembling
the
live
material
so
soon
after
Cobain's
death
to
be
too
emotionally
overwhelming.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
the
career-spanning
live
portion
postponed,
<i><a
href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged_in_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Unplugged
in
New
York">MTV
Unplugged
in
New
York</a></i>
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
charts
upon
release
in
November
1994.
A
few
weeks
later
the
group's
first
full-length
video,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live!_Tonight!_Sold_Out!!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live!
Tonight!
Sold
Out!!">Live!
Tonight!
Sold
Out!!</a></i>,
was
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-goldmine_55-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goldmine-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
following
year,
<i>MTV
Unplugged
in
New
York</i>
earned
Nirvana
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Music
Album">Best
Alternative
Music
Album</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1996
DGC
finally
issued
a
Nirvana
live
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/From_the_Muddy_Banks_of_the_Wishkah?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="From
the
Muddy
Banks
of
the
Wishkah">From
the
Muddy
Banks
of
the
Wishkah</a></i>,
which
became
the
third
Nirvana
release
in
a
row
to
debut
at
the
top
of
the
<i>Billboard</i>
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-goldmine_55-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-goldmine-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1997,
Novoselic,
Grohl,
and
Courtney
Love
formed
the
<a
href="/wiki/Limited_liability_corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Limited
liability
corporation"
class="mw-redirect">limited
liability
corporation</a>
Nirvana
LLC
to
oversee
all
Nirvana-related
projects.<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
45-track
box
set
of
Nirvana
rarities
was
scheduled
for
release
in
October
2001.<sup
id="cite_ref-Heath_77-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Heath-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
shortly
before
the
release
date,
Love
filed
a
suit
to
dissolve
Nirvana
LLC,
and
an
injunction
was
issued
preventing
the
release
of
any
new
Nirvana
material
until
the
case
was
resolved.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
Love
contended
that
Cobain
was
the
band,
that
Grohl
and
Novoselic
were
sidemen,
and
that
she
signed
the
partnership
agreement
originally
under
bad
advice.
Grohl
and
Novoselic
countersued,
asking
the
court
to
remove
Love
from
the
partnership
and
to
replace
her
with
another
representative
of
Cobain's
estate.<sup
id="cite_ref-Heath_77-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Heath-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
day
before
the
case
was
set
to
go
to
trial
in
October
2002,
Love,
Novoselic,
and
Grohl
announced
that
they
had
reached
a
settlement.
The
settlement
paved
the
way
for
the
release
of
the
compilation
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(Nirvana_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(Nirvana
album)">Nirvana</a></i>,
which
featured
the
previously
unreleased
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Know_You%27re_Right?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Know
You're
Right">You
Know
You're
Right</a>&quot;,
the
last
song
Nirvana
recorded
before
Cobain's
death.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Nirvana</i>
was
released
later
that
month,
debuting
at
number
three
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
box
set,
<i><a
href="/wiki/With_the_Lights_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="With
the
Lights
Out">With
the
Lights
Out</a></i>,
was
finally
released
in
November
2004.
The
release
contained
a
vast
array
of
early
Cobain
demos,
rough
rehearsal
recordings,
and
live
tracks
recorded
throughout
the
band's
history.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sliver:_The_Best_of_the_Box?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sliver:
The
Best
of
the
Box"
class="mw-redirect">Sliver:
The
Best
of
the
Box</a></i>,
which
culled
19
tracks
from
the
box
set
in
addition
to
featuring
three
previously
unreleased
tracks,
was
released
in
late
2005.<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
April
2006,
Love
announced
that
she
had
arranged
to
sell
25
percent
of
her
stake
in
the
Nirvana
song
catalog
in
a
deal
estimated
at
$50
million.
The
share
of
Nirvana's
publishing
was
purchased
by
Primary
Wave
Music,
which
was
founded
by
Larry
Mestel,
a
former
CEO
of
<a
href="/wiki/Virgin_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Virgin
Records">Virgin
Records</a>.
In
an
accompanying
statement,
Love
sought
to
assure
Nirvana's
fanbase
that
the
music
would
not
simply
be
licensed
to
the
highest
bidder,
noting,
&quot;We
are
going
to
remain
very
tasteful
and
true
to
the
spirit
of
Nirvana
while
taking
the
music
to
places
it
has
never
been
before.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup>
Further
releases
have
since
been
made.
This
includes
the
DVD
releases
of
<i>Live!
Tonight!
Sold
Out!!</i>
in
2006,<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
full,
uncut
version
of
<i>MTV
Unplugged
in
New
York</i>
in
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
performance
at
the
1992
Reading
Festival
was
released
on
both
CD
and
DVD
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_at_Reading?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
at
Reading">Live
at
Reading</a></i>
in
November
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
month,
Sub
Pop
released
a
20th
anniversary
deluxe
edition
of
<i>Bleach</i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-pitchfork_86-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pitchfork-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
DGC
released
a
number
of
20th
anniversary
deluxe-edition
packages
of
both
<i>Nevermind</i>
in
September
2011<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<i>In
Utero</i>
in
September
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2012,
Grohl,
Novoselic,
and
Smear
joined
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
McCartney">Paul
McCartney</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="12-12-12:
The
Concert
for
Sandy
Relief">12-12-12:
The
Concert
for
Sandy
Relief</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
performance
featured
the
premiere
of
a
new
song
written
by
the
four
musicians
entitled
&quot;Cut
Me
Some
Slack&quot;.
A
studio
recording
was
released
on
the
soundtrack
to
<a
href="/wiki/Sound_City_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
City
(film)"><i>Sound
City</i></a>,
a
film
by
Grohl.<sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic-sound-city_91-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-sound-city-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
July
19,
2013,
they
would
once
again
play
with
McCartney
during
the
encore
of
his
<a
href="/wiki/Safeco_Field?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Safeco
Field">Safeco
Field</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Out_There!_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Out
There!
Tour">&quot;Out
There&quot;</a>
concert
in
Seattle,
the
first
time
Nirvana
members
played
together
in
their
hometown
in
over
15
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style">Musical
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style">edit</a>]</span></h2>

of
&quot;Smells

<i><a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nevermind">Nevermind</a></i>
(1991).
Nirvana
utilized
dynamic
contrasts
in
its
music,
present
in
this
song
in
the
form
of
a
sparse
two-note
guitar
verse
guitar
melody
and
choruses
of

<a

chords</a>.

<tr>











<td
colspan="2"
class="mbox-text"
style="line-height:1.1em;"><span
style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems
playing
this
file?
