<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Media
help">media
help</a>.</i></span></td>










</tr>









</tbody>







</table>








<p>Cobain
described
the
sound
of
Nirvana
when
it
first
started
as
&quot;a
<a
href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gang
of
Four
(band)">Gang
of
Four</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Scratch_Acid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scratch
Acid">Scratch
Acid</a>
ripoff&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Azerrad.2C_1994._p._294_56-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Azerrad.2C_1994._p._294-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
Later
when
Nirvana
recorded
<i>Bleach</i>,
Cobain
felt
he
had
to
fit
the
expectations
of
the
Sub
Pop
grunge
sound
to
build
a
fanbase,
and
hence
suppressed
his
arty
and
pop
songwriting
traits
while
crafting
the
record
in
favor
of
a
more
rocking
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-Az_102_95-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Az_102-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nirvana
biographer
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Azerrad?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Azerrad">Michael
Azerrad</a>
argued,
&quot;Ironically,
it
was
the
restrictions
of
the
Sub
Pop
sound
that
helped
the
band
find
its
musical
identity&quot;.
Azerrad
stated
that
by
acknowledging
that
its
members
had
grown
up
listening
to
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Sabbath">Black
Sabbath</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>,
the
band
was
able
to
move
on
from
its
derivative
early
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-96"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Nirvana
used
dynamic
shifts
that
went
from
quiet
to
loud.<sup
id="cite_ref-FrickeRS1994_64-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FrickeRS1994-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
had
sought
to
mix
heavy
and
pop
musical
sounds;
he
commented,
&quot;I
wanted
to
be
totally
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>
in
a
way
and
then
be
totally
extreme
punk
rock
and
then
do
real
wimpy
pop
songs&quot;.
When
Cobain
heard
the
<a
href="/wiki/Pixies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pixies">Pixies</a>'
1988
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Surfer_Rosa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surfer
Rosa">Surfer
Rosa</a></i>
after
recording
<i>Bleach</i>,
he
felt
it
had
the
sound
he
wanted
to
achieve
but
until
then
was
too
intimidated
to
try.
The
Pixies'
subsequent
popularity
encouraged
Cobain
to
follow
his
instincts
as
a
songwriter.<sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
Like
the
Pixies,
Nirvana
moved
between
&quot;spare
bass-and-drum
grooves
and
shrill
bursts
of
screaming
guitar
and
vocals&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup>
Near
the
end
of
his
life,
Cobain
noted
the
band
had
become
bored
by
the
formula,
finding
it
limited,
but
he
expressed
doubts
that
the
band
was
skilled
enough
to
try
other
dynamics.<sup
id="cite_ref-FrickeRS1994_64-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FrickeRS1994-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Cobain's
rhythm
guitar
style,
which
relied
on
power
chords,
low-note
riffs,
and
a
loose
right-hand
technique,
featured
the
key
components
to
the
band’s
songs.
Cobain
would
often
initially
play
a
song's
verse
riff
in
a
clean
tone,
then
double
it
with
distorted
guitars
when
he
repeated
the
part.
In
some
songs
the
guitar
would
be
absent
from
the
verses
entirely
to
allow
the
drums
and
bass
guitar
to
support
the
vocals,
or
it
would
only
play
sparse
melodies
like
the
two-note
pattern
used
in
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;.
Cobain
rarely
played
standard
guitar
solos,
opting
to
play
slight
variations
of
the
song's
melody
as
single
note
lines.
Cobain's
solos
were
mostly
blues-based
and
out
of
tune,
which
music
writer
Jon
Chappell
described
as
&quot;almost
an
iconoclastic
parody
of
the
traditional
instrumental
break&quot;,
a
quality
typified
by
the
note-for-note
replication
of
the
lead
melody
in
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;
and
the
atonal
solo
for
&quot;Breed&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Chappel_94-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Chappel-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Grohl's
drumming
&quot;took
Nirvana's
sound
to
a
new
level
of
intensity&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
Azerrad
stated
that
Grohl's
&quot;powerful
drumming
propelled
the
band
to
a
whole
new
plane,
visually
as
well
as
musically&quot;,
noting,
&quot;Although
Dave
is
a
merciless
basher,
his
parts
are
also
distinctly
musical—it
wouldn't
be
difficult
to
figure
out
what
song
he
was
playing
even
without
the
rest
of
the
music.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
live
performances,
Cobain
and
Novoselic
would
always
tune
their
guitars
to
E
flat.<sup
id="cite_ref-requiem_101-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-requiem-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
noted,
&quot;We
play
so
hard
we
can't
tune
our
guitars
fast
enough.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-cheaptricks_102-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cheaptricks-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
made
a
habit
of
destroying
its
equipment
after
shows.
Novoselic
said
he
and
Cobain
created
the
&quot;shtick&quot;
in
order
to
get
off
of
the
stage
sooner.<sup
id="cite_ref-classicalbums_103-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-classicalbums-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
stated
it
began
as
an
expression
of
his
frustration
with
Chad
Channing
making
mistakes
and
dropping
out
entirely
during
performances.<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Songwriting_and_lyrics">Songwriting
and
lyrics</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Songwriting
and
lyrics">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Everett_True?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Everett
True">Everett
True</a>
said
in
1989,
&quot;Nirvana
songs
treat
the
banal
and
pedestrian
with
a
unique
slant.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-105"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
came
up
with
the
basic
components
of
each
song
(usually
writing
them
on
an
acoustic
guitar),
as
well
as
the
singing
style
and
the
lyrics.
He
emphasized
that
Novoselic
and
Grohl
&quot;have
a
big
part
in
deciding
on
how
long
a
song
should
be
and
how
many
parts
it
should
have.
So
I
don't
like
to
be
considered
the
sole
songwriter.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-making_Nevermind_106-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-making_Nevermind-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
asked
which
part
of
the
songs
he
would
write
first,
Cobain
responded,
&quot;I
don’t
know.
I
really
don’t
know.
I
guess
I
start
with
the
verse
and
then
go
into
the
chorus.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FrickeRS1994_64-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FrickeRS1994-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Cobain
usually
wrote
lyrics
for
songs
minutes
before
recording
them.<sup
id="cite_ref-making_Nevermind_106-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-making_Nevermind-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
said,
&quot;When
I
write
a
song
the
lyrics
are
the
least
important
subject.
I
can
go
through
two
or
three
different
subjects
in
a
song
and
the
title
can
mean
absolutely
nothing
at
all.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spin
(magazine)">Spin</a></i>
in
1993
that
he
&quot;didn't
give
a
flying
fuck&quot;
what
the
lyrics
on
<i>Bleach</i>
were
about,
figuring
&quot;Let's
just
scream
some
negative
lyrics
and
as
long
as
they're
not
sexist
and
don't
get
too
embarrassing
it'll
be
okay&quot;,
while
the
lyrics
to
<i>Nevermind</i>
were
taken
from
two
years
of
poetry
he
had
accumulated,
which
he
cut
up
and
chose
lines
he
preferred
from.
In
comparison,
Cobain
stated
that
the
lyrics
to
<i>In
Utero</i>
were
&quot;more
focused,
they're
almost
built
on
themes&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-smashing_108-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-smashing-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cobain
didn't
write
necessarily
in
a
linear
fashion,
instead
relying
on
juxtapositions
of
contradictory
images
to
convey
emotions
and
ideas.
Often
in
his
lyrics,
Cobain
would
present
an
idea
then
reject
it;
the
songwriter
explained,
&quot;I'm
such
a
nihilistic
jerk
half
the
time
and
other
times
I'm
so
vulnerable
and
sincere
[.
.
.
The
songs
are]
like
a
mixture
of
both
of
them.
That's
how
most
people
my
age
are.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Legacy">Legacy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Legacy">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
boilerplate
seealso">








See
also:









<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044#Popularization_in_the_1990s"
title="Alternative
rock">Alternative
rock:
Popularization
in
the
1990s</a>







</div>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine">Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine</a>
wrote
that
prior
to
Nirvana,
&quot;alternative
music
was
consigned
to
specialty
sections
of
record
stores,
and
major
labels
considered
it
to
be,
at
the
very
most,
a
tax
write-off&quot;.
Following
the
release
of
<i>Nevermind</i>,
&quot;nothing
was
ever
quite
the
same,
for
better
and
for
worse&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nirvana_bio_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nirvana_bio-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
success
of
<i>Nevermind</i>
not
only
popularized
grunge,
but
also
established
&quot;the
cultural
and
commercial
viability
of
alternative
rock
in
general&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-10_years_later_110-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10_years_later-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
other
alternative
bands
had
had
hits
before,
Nirvana
&quot;broke
down
the
doors
forever&quot;,
according
to
Erlewine.
Erlewine
further
stated
that
Nirvana's
breakthrough
&quot;didn't
eliminate
the
underground&quot;,
but
rather
&quot;just
gave
it
more
exposure&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-American_altrock_111-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-American_altrock-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1992,
<a
href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Pareles">Jon
Pareles</a>
of
<i>The
New
York
Times</i>
reported
that
Nirvana's
breakthrough
had
made
others
in
the
alternative
scene
impatient
for
achieving
similar
success,
noting,
&quot;Suddenly,
all
bets
are
off.
No
one
has
the
inside
track
on
which
of
dozens,
perhaps
hundreds,
of
ornery,
obstreperous,
unkempt
bands
might
next
appeal
to
the
mall-walking
millions&quot;.
Record
company
executives
offered
large
advances
and
record
deals
to
bands,
and
previous
strategies
of
building
audiences
for
alternative
rock
groups
had
been
replaced
by
the
opportunity
to
achieve
mainstream
popularity
quickly.<sup
id="cite_ref-112"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Erlewine
stated
that
Nirvana's
breakthrough
&quot;popularized
so-called
'<a
href="/wiki/Generation_X?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Generation
X">Generation
X</a>'
and
'slacker'
culture&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-American_altrock_111-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-American_altrock-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
Immediately
following
Cobain's
death,
numerous
headlines
referred
to
Nirvana's
frontman
as
&quot;the
voice
of
a
generation&quot;,
although
he
had
rejected
such
labeling
during
his
lifetime.<sup
id="cite_ref-113"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup>
Reflecting
on
Cobain's
death
over
ten
years
later,
<a
href="/wiki/MSNBC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a>'s
Eric
Olsen
wrote,
&quot;In
the
intervening
decade,
Cobain,
a
small,
frail
but
handsome
man
in
life,
has
become
an
abstract
Generation
X
icon,
viewed
by
many
as
the
'last
real
rock
star'
[.
.
.]
a
messiah
and
martyr
whose
every
utterance
has
been
plundered
and
parsed&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-10_years_later_110-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10_years_later-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards
and
accolades</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Nirvana_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Awards
and
accolades">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Nirvana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Nirvana">List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Nirvana</a>







</div>








<p>Since
its
breakup,
Nirvana
has
continued
to
receive
acclaim,
and
is
regularly
considered
one
of
the
greatest
music
artists
of
all
time.
In
2003,
Nirvana
was
selected
as
one
of
the
inductees
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Mojo_Collection?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Mojo
Collection"
class="mw-redirect"><i>Mojo</i>
Hall
of
Fame
100</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-114"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
received
a
nomination
for
induction
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Music
Hall
of
Fame">UK
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2004
as
the
&quot;Greatest
Artist
of
the
1990s&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-115"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
placed
Nirvana
at
number
27
on
their
list
of
the
&quot;100
Greatest
Artists
of
All
Time&quot;
in
2004,<sup
id="cite_ref-116"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
at
number
30
on
their
updated
list
in
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-117"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2003,
the
magazine's
senior
editor
<a
href="/wiki/David_Fricke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Fricke">David
Fricke</a>
picked
Kurt
Cobain
as
the
12th
best
guitarist
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-118"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
later
ranked
Cobain
as
the
45th
greatest
singer
in
2008<sup
id="cite_ref-119"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
73rd
greatest
guitarist
of
all
time
in
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-120"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>
ranked
Nirvana
as
the
42nd
greatest
artists
of
rock
and
roll
in
1998,<sup
id="cite_ref-121"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
7th
greatest
hard
rock
artists
in
2000,<sup
id="cite_ref-122"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
14th
greatest
artists
of
all
time
in
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-123"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Nirvana's
contributions
to
music
have
also
received
recognition,
with
<i>Nevermind</i>
and
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;
consistently
being
ranked
as
one
of
the
greatest
albums
and
songs
of
all
time,
respectively.
The
Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame
has
inducted
two
of
Nirvana's
recordings,
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;
and
&quot;All
Apologies&quot;,
into
its
list
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044#.22The_Songs_That_Shaped_Rock_and_Roll.22"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">The
Songs
That
Shaped
Rock
and
Roll</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-124"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
museum
also
ranked
<i>Nevermind</i>
number
10
on
its
&quot;The
Definitive
200
Albums
of
All
Time&quot;
list
in
2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-125"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2005,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Library
of
Congress">Library
of
Congress</a>
added
<i>Nevermind</i>
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/National_Recording_Registry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Recording
Registry">National
Recording
Registry</a>,
which
collects
&quot;culturally,
historically
or
aesthetically
important&quot;
sound
recordings
from
the
20th
century.<sup
id="cite_ref-126"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2011,
four
of
Nirvana's
songs
appeared
on
<i>Rolling
Stone</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
updated
list
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Songs_of_All_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone's
500
Greatest
Songs
of
All
Time">The
500
Greatest
Songs
of
All
Time</a>&quot;,
with
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;
ranking
the
highest
at
number
9.<sup
id="cite_ref-500_Songs_127-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-500_Songs-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
Three
of
the
band's
albums
were
ranked
on
the
magazine's
2012
list
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone's
500
Greatest
Albums
of
All
Time">The
500
Greatest
Albums
of
All
Time</a>&quot;,
with
<i>Nevermind</i>
placing
the
highest
at
number
17.<sup
id="cite_ref-500_Albums_128-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-500_Albums-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
same
three
Nirvana
albums
were
also
placed
on
<i>Rolling
Stone'</i>s
2011
list
of
&quot;The
100
Best
Albums
of
the
Nineties&quot;,
with
<i>Nevermind</i>
ranking
the
highest
at
number
1,
making
it
the
greatest
album
of
the
decade.<sup
id="cite_ref-100_Albums_1990s_129-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100_Albums_1990s-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Time</i>
included
<i>Nevermind</i>
on
its
list
of
&quot;The
All-TIME
100
Albums&quot;
in
2006,
labeling
it
&quot;the
finest
album
of
the
90s.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-130"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2011,
the
magazine
also
added
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;
on
its
list
of
&quot;The
All-TIME
100
Songs&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-131"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
&quot;Heart-Shaped
Box&quot;
on
its
list
of
&quot;The
30
All-TIME
Best
Music
Videos&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-132"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Nirvana
are
one
of
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">the
best-selling
bands</a>
of
all
time,
having
sold
over
75
million
records
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-133"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
over
25&nbsp;million
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
Industry
Association
of
America">RIAA</a>-certified
units,
they
are
also
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists_in_the_United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists
in
the
United
States">the
80th
best-selling
music
artist
in
the
United
States</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-134"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
of
the
band's
studio
albums
and
two
of
their
live
albums
have
reached
the
top
spot
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-135"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nirvana
has
been
awarded
one
Diamond,
three
Multi-Platinum,
seven
Platinum
and
one
Gold
<a
href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
recording
sales
certification">certified
albums</a>
in
the
United
States
by
the
RIAA,<sup
id="cite_ref-136"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
four
Multi-Platinum,
four
Platinum,
two
Gold
and
one
Silver
certified
albums
in
the
UK
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="British
Phonographic
Industry">BPI</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-137"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Nevermind</i>,
the
band's
most
successful
album,
has
sold
over
30
million
copies
worldwide,
making
it
one
of
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
albums">the
best-selling
albums</a>
ever.<sup
id="cite_ref-138"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
most
successful
song,
&quot;Smells
Like
Teen
Spirit&quot;,
is
among
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
singles">the
best-selling
singles</a>
of
all
time,
having
sold
8
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-139"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Nirvana
were
announced
in
their
first
year
of
eligibility
as
being
part
of
the
2014
class
of
inductees
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
on
December
17,
2013.
The
induction
ceremony
will
be
held
April
10,
2014
in
Brooklyn,
NY
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Barclays_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barclays
Center">Barclays
Center</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-140"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Nirvana_%28band%29&page=1&ac=24&qid=5EA05419F98E68CC492478B00741418E&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();
